  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_8a1544cf-aad1-4e42-9bba-32d6c35de895'
      });
    }

      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"
      loadScript(APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL, initAppleId);
    };

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2977324141" />
    <a title="Kate Willis" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/56441586-kate-willis"><img alt="Kate Willis" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1598855553p2/56441586.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2977324141?book_show_action=true">Sep 16, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kate Willis" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kate Willis" href="/user/show/56441586-kate-willis">Kate Willis</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback " href="/book/show/25134664-the-mysterious-benedict-society-and-the-prisoner-s-dilemma">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/56441586-kate-willis?shelf=adoption-foster-care">adoption-foster-care</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/56441586-kate-willis?shelf=buddy-read">buddy-read</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/56441586-kate-willis?shelf=contemporary">contemporary</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/56441586-kate-willis?shelf=mystery">mystery</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/56441586-kate-willis?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/56441586-kate-willis?shelf=dystopian">dystopian</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/56441586-kate-willis?shelf=great-siblings">great-siblings</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2977324141" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10050400711583933346">Once upon a time, I was ordering birthday gifts and this was on sale so I bought it for myself and lived happily ever after. The End.<br/><br/>This book got to travel around with me a bit more than books usually do which probably is a testament to how good it was. XD <br/><br/>I ate up every clever and heart-filled moment of this book. I especially enjoyed moments when the Society was working together and Constance’s backstory. (Seriously, wow. I never expected to get to know it, but when we did, it made soooo much</span>
  <span id="freeText10050400711583933346" style="display:none">Once upon a time, I was ordering birthday gifts and this was on sale so I bought it for myself and lived happily ever after. The End.<br /><br />This book got to travel around with me a bit more than books usually do which probably is a testament to how good it was. XD <br /><br />I ate up every clever and heart-filled moment of this book. I especially enjoyed moments when the Society was working together and Constance’s backstory. (Seriously, wow. I never expected to get to know it, but when we did, it made soooo much sense.)<br /><br />Mr. Benedict completely wrecked my heart in this one. He was so giving and selfless and brave. Reynie was great too, as always, and everyone. Constance was fun as a satire of a typical little kid--noticing patterns, getting her way, and subtly letting adults know what she needs. <br /><br />Something I especially loved in this book (and the whole series, really) is the family relationships both by blood and adoption. Don’t get me started on the amazing loyalty between Kate and her dad, Milligan. Also, the Washingtons and Sticky are sweet, and even though I relate to him least of all, Sticky <i>is</i> growing on me and it’s neat to see his character develop. There was even a hint of this sort of relationship on the evil side which was surprising and interesting… So much love and trust and loyalty in this book. (I mean, I should have expected that from the title. XD )<br /><br />It ended on a truly triumphant note, and I’m so glad to have read this series. &lt;3<br /><br />Just a note, the Ten Men can be very threatening, and there are injuries, kidnappings, and a lot of general peril on about the same level as the other books. <br /><br />Best quote: Reynie felt an old, familiar ache. He instantly recognized it as loneliness--or in this case anticipated loneliness--and not for the first time he lamented his too-vivid imagination. <br /><br />(And then there’s the beautiful sentence about Milligan on pg. 337, but it’s a spoiler, sweetie.)<br /><br />Altogether, this was quite satisfying, and I understand now why this is well-beloved. ;)<br /><br />It remains to be seen whether or not I’ll read the prequel and the new book. ;)</span>
  <a data-text-id="10050400711583933346" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer9232144131044038252"> I really loved the first book in this series, the second a bit less, and this third one by far the least. <br/> It's got the same characters I loved before, but now they are no longer regular, clever kids - Sticky sits down to memorize the entire library catalog in case they need it, Reynie starts to have some mysterious sixth sense where he can sense something is wrong, and Constance, this one killed me-she's venturing into Obi-Wan Kenobi territory by reading minds and pulling Jedi mind tricks. My </span>
  <span id="freeText9232144131044038252" style="display:none"> I really loved the first book in this series, the second a bit less, and this third one by far the least. <br /> It's got the same characters I loved before, but now they are no longer regular, clever kids - Sticky sits down to memorize the entire library catalog in case they need it, Reynie starts to have some mysterious sixth sense where he can sense something is wrong, and Constance, this one killed me-she's venturing into Obi-Wan Kenobi territory by reading minds and pulling Jedi mind tricks. My favorite Kate is even a little far fetched this time, how she moves with super human speed and can throw a flashlight in the dark with deadly accuracy. <i>Really?</i><br /> Even Milligan, the master of disguise who always comes out on the right end of a fight, is tiresome. Can't he bring more than a boomerang as a weapon? <br /> The whole thing got long and increasingly silly and I was disappointed with this last book in the series. </span>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/78064678" />

      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="ebook 9780316072465" href="/book/show/6979808-the-mysterious-benedict-society-and-the-prisoner-s-dilemma">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2172094-kat-drennan-scace?shelf=borrowed">borrowed</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2172094-kat-drennan-scace?shelf=childrens">childrens</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer78064678" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14855109995873428336"><br/>The third book in the Mysterious Benedict Society series, is pretty much perfect. We solve all sorts of mysteries like Constance's past and Number Two's real name while trying to stop Mr. Curtain at the same time. <br/><br/>I love how these books are so smartly written. He doesn't write down to children at all. There's so much conflict and a lot of it isn't even Big Bad conflict, it's bureaucracy and government red tape. They're, for lack of a better word, grown-up problems, the kind that make you really </span>
  <span id="freeText14855109995873428336" style="display:none"><br />The third book in the Mysterious Benedict Society series, is pretty much perfect. We solve all sorts of mysteries like Constance's past and Number Two's real name while trying to stop Mr. Curtain at the same time. <br /><br />I love how these books are so smartly written. He doesn't write down to children at all. There's so much conflict and a lot of it isn't even Big Bad conflict, it's bureaucracy and government red tape. They're, for lack of a better word, grown-up problems, the kind that make you really frustrated. <br /><br />I love books where things seem so hopeless, so ridiculously tangled that you think, 'how the heck are they going to manage to get out of this in the next 100 pages?' and then, because it's a children's book, they do and not only do they get out of it, they get out of it in a way that is clever and makes sense for the characters involved. <br /><br />If you haven't picked up the series, I'd definitely recommend it. As I said above, it's really clever children's literature. </span>
  <a data-text-id="14855109995873428336" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_274979038" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/274979038" />
    <a title="Annette" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1426170-annette"><img alt="Annette" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1401252164p2/1426170.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/274979038?book_show_action=true">Feb 09, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Annette" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Annette" href="/user/show/1426170-annette">Annette</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1426170-annette?shelf=sci-fi">sci-fi</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1426170-annette?shelf=youth">youth</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer274979038" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11993110627872420528">A fun, fast read, even for adults. However, I cannot pretend that it is anywhere as good as <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/83369.The_Mysterious_Benedict_Society__Mysterious_Benedict_Society___1_' title='The Mysterious Benedict Society (Mysterious Benedict Society, #1) by Trenton Lee Stewart' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Mysterious Benedict Society</a>, or even quite as good as book #2, <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/2159225.The_Mysterious_Benedict_Society_and_the_Perilous_Journey__Mysterious_Benedict_Society___2_' title='The Mysterious Benedict Society and the Perilous Journey (Mysterious Benedict Society, #2) by Trenton Lee Stewart' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Mysterious Benedict Society and the Perilous Journey</a>. The situations are increasingly strained as far as believability, as well as being simply less weighty than the original book's. Certain elements - Mr. Benedict's narcolepsy at inopportune moments, Milligan's ridiculous tendency towards injury, etc - are becoming rather rote at this</span>
  <span id="freeText11993110627872420528" style="display:none">A fun, fast read, even for adults. However, I cannot pretend that it is anywhere as good as <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/83369.The_Mysterious_Benedict_Society__Mysterious_Benedict_Society___1_" title="The Mysterious Benedict Society (Mysterious Benedict Society, #1) by Trenton Lee Stewart" rel="nofollow noopener">The Mysterious Benedict Society</a>, or even quite as good as book #2, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/2159225.The_Mysterious_Benedict_Society_and_the_Perilous_Journey__Mysterious_Benedict_Society___2_" title="The Mysterious Benedict Society and the Perilous Journey (Mysterious Benedict Society, #2) by Trenton Lee Stewart" rel="nofollow noopener">The Mysterious Benedict Society and the Perilous Journey</a>. The situations are increasingly strained as far as believability, as well as being simply less weighty than the original book's. Certain elements - Mr. Benedict's narcolepsy at inopportune moments, Milligan's ridiculous tendency towards injury, etc - are becoming rather rote at this point. Still, it's enjoyable - I get a kick out of the silly names like the silver-haired "Ms. Argent" and the grasping "Covett S. Gaines." <br />We'll see if the author can improve the series in future books. </span>

<div id="review_551549700" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/551549700" />
    <a title="Ella" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/18024468-ella"><img alt="Ella" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/u_50x66-632230dc9882b4352d753eedf9396530.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/551549700?book_show_action=true">Mar 03, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Ella" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Ella" href="/user/show/18024468-ella">Ella</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer551549700" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15280597300021421176">When Constance finds out that she is adopted, she runs away out of sadness. She can’t control her emotions, and can’t think of anything else to do. All the grownups in the house go out on a search party to find her, leaving Kate, Sticky and Reynie home alone. All seems well until a mysterious vehicle arrives at the house. They soon find out that Mr Curtain is out to capture them. The children attempt to run away. In the process, they find Constance but unfortunately get captured as well. They ge</span>
  <span id="freeText15280597300021421176" style="display:none">When Constance finds out that she is adopted, she runs away out of sadness. She can’t control her emotions, and can’t think of anything else to do. All the grownups in the house go out on a search party to find her, leaving Kate, Sticky and Reynie home alone. All seems well until a mysterious vehicle arrives at the house. They soon find out that Mr Curtain is out to capture them. The children attempt to run away. In the process, they find Constance but unfortunately get captured as well. They get taken to an abandoned prison, where Constance is able to send “mental messages” to Mr Benedict. He soon finds them, and through all the children’s teamwork, they manage to escape, and send Mr Curtain and the Ten Men to jail.<br /><br /><br />One theme in my book was power. I think this theme was very important, because Mr Benedict and Mr Curtain both had the power to run a very important machine – The Whisperer. The Whisperer was a machine that could control other people’s minds, and if it got into the wrong hands, it could do a lot of damage. Mr Curtain was the antagonist, therefore he wanted to rule the world, and control people’s minds. Mr Benedict was trying to prevent him from doing this. Mr Curtain also “ruled” certain people, and had a lot of power over them. A quote from the book that shows power is “S.Q.! Come to the rear end of the prison at once – at once S.Q.! Do not make me –““But?” Mr Curtain snapped. “But? You may not say ‘but’ to me, S.Q. Pedelian!” This quote shows power because Mr Curtain obviously ruled over S.Q., and didn't like him very much.<br /><br />Another theme that shows in the book is rivalry. I think this theme was very important, because there was lots of rivalry between Mr Benedict and Mr Curtain. They were long lost identical twins, but had completely different minds and personalities. They were against each other. Mr Curtain wanted to rule the world and brainwash people, but Mr Benedict was trying to stop him from doing that. A quote that shows rivalry is “How dare you tell me when anything is finished, Benedict? No! No! No! I shall tell you when it is over right now!” And flipping a switch on his wheelchair, he glared at Mr Benedict with such hideous intensity that it was alarming even to look at his face. (Page 354) This quote shows rivalry, because Mr Curtain was getting mad at Mr Benedict, and clearly hates his brother.<br /><br />Another theme in the book was teamwork. This occurred most in the book, because the whole book was about trying to work as a team, and the children had to work together to escape Mr Curtain. One quote that shows teamwork is “I’m not counting on me this time, I promise. I’m counting on us.”(Page 281) This quote shows teamwork because Kate knew that she couldn’t do it by herself, but she needed the others as well. <br /><br /><br /><br />I thought my book was engaging because it used very descriptive language. There were many words that I had never heard before, and enjoyed learning, and trying to remember the meanings. Some examples of descriptive words that I learned were: bureaucratic, egomaniac, and naïveté. I had never heard some of these words before, and I learned the meanings! <br /><br /><br />I think this book is good for a 6th or 7th grader. I think it is a good book because most of the time it was captivating. For example when one chapter was finished, it would sometimes be a cliff-hanger, and leave you wondering what would happen next. I think this is a very good style of writing because it makes you want to read more, and you can’t put the book down. These bits in the book were very exciting, but sometimes the book got a bit boring. The story would slow down, and nothing much would be happening. Luckily, soon the story would pick up again, and make you want more. Another good aspect of the story (as I already said) was it had many descriptive words. The story was filled with vocabulary, and made you want to learn the definition! This means that the book was also somewhat educational as well as exhilarating.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="15280597300021421176" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_129961765" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/129961765" />
    <a title="Dixie Thamrin" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3511392-dixie-thamrin"><img alt="Dixie Thamrin" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1289324117p2/3511392.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/129961765?book_show_action=true">Nov 09, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Dixie Thamrin" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Dixie Thamrin" href="/user/show/3511392-dixie-thamrin">Dixie Thamrin</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780316045506" href="/book/show/6973518-the-mysterious-benedict-society-and-the-prisoner-s-dilemma">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
                  <em>
                    This review has been hidden because it contains spoilers. To view it,
                    <a href="#" onclick="Effect.toggle(&#39;reviewTextContainer129961765&#39;); return false;">click here.</a>
                  </em>
              <span id="reviewTextContainer129961765" class="readable"
                    style="display:none"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16827923069861238241">Prepare yourself for another wild yet amazing adventure! This time Reynie, Sticky, Kate, and Constance are back again to save The Whisperer from its wicked inventor, Mr. Leodroptha Curtain. <br/><br/>The story begins with an explanation of the prisoner's dilemma, which I found quite interesting. The problem started when Constance was missing. Her runaway was followed by a total blackout in the town, causing chaos everywhere. The chaos was used by Mr. Curtain and his gang, The Executive, to trap the childr</span>
  <span id="freeText16827923069861238241" style="display:none">Prepare yourself for another wild yet amazing adventure! This time Reynie, Sticky, Kate, and Constance are back again to save The Whisperer from its wicked inventor, Mr. Leodroptha Curtain. <br /><br />The story begins with an explanation of the prisoner's dilemma, which I found quite interesting. The problem started when Constance was missing. Her runaway was followed by a total blackout in the town, causing chaos everywhere. The chaos was used by Mr. Curtain and his gang, The Executive, to trap the children with findable clues and breakable codes. Unfortunately, the children got into the trap and they were kidnapped.<br /><br />When they found out that they were brought to a faraway prison that was under renovation, they began to set some tricks to get out. Again, the luck wasn't on their side. The Executive found them and locked them again in a tower. Not running out of ideas, Constance used her ability to send the news by vision to Mr. Benedict, and she got a vision back from him, telling her that he and all the agents would save them.<br /><br />Okay, I won't tell you the rest of the story. All I can say is, this book is <i>breathtaking</i>. It reminds me of Harry Potter and the Order of Phoenix, where Harry and his friends were got into Voldemort's trap (just like the children were got into Mr. Curtain's trap), fought against the Death Eater and Voldemort himself (in this case, The Executive and Mr. Curtain), and got help from the members of the Order of Phoenix (just like the children got help from Mr. Benedict's agent). The difference between Harry Potter and the Order of Phoenix and this book is, it's MUCH better than Harry Potter, because no one died in the end and they all had happy endings.<br /><br />I should give the author more credit, though, for making such genius riddles in this book. The riddles were brilliantly made, and it definitely adds to the excitement. I read the riddles and couldn't stop wondering the answers, and when they were revealed, I was flabbergasted. They're just smart, genius, and brilliant!<br /><br />When I finished reading this book, I felt some satisfaction. What satisfaction? Well, when when everything turned out to be okay, it's enough to make me satisfied. I recommend you to read the two previous books before reading this one, or you'll get confused because the story is continual.<br /><br />Happy reading and enjoy the adventure!</span>
  <a data-text-id="16827923069861238241" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_83304476" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/83304476" />
    <a title="Alicia" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1577641-alicia"><img alt="Alicia" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1362550383p2/1577641.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/83304476?book_show_action=true">Jan 04, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Alicia" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Alicia" href="/user/show/1577641-alicia">Alicia</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer83304476" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2168710708588650392">It just keeps getting more and more ridiculous. In a world where grown men electroshock small children, hit them on the head with pipes and threaten to break their legs, NO ONE THINKS TO BRING A GUN. What do they bring to combat electricity shooting masochists? Rubber gloves (that can defy physics and REPEL electricity. Yeah, I know, lame) and their other tool. A boomerang. <br/><br/>It's like a bad episode of MacGyver. "Oh no, MacGyver, there's only 35 seconds on the bomb. What will you do? It's ok, I ju</span>
  <span id="freeText2168710708588650392" style="display:none">It just keeps getting more and more ridiculous. In a world where grown men electroshock small children, hit them on the head with pipes and threaten to break their legs, NO ONE THINKS TO BRING A GUN. What do they bring to combat electricity shooting masochists? Rubber gloves (that can defy physics and REPEL electricity. Yeah, I know, lame) and their other tool. A boomerang. <br /><br />It's like a bad episode of MacGyver. "Oh no, MacGyver, there's only 35 seconds on the bomb. What will you do? It's ok, I just hand me your left earring, that shoelace and a piece of bubble gum. I'll have us out of here in 12 seconds" <br /><br />And then for some reason, the "baddens" keep leaving these children alone. Children who are geniuses, who have shown remarkable talent for escape and planning before. Why would someone do that? It reminds me of Austin Powers when this takes place:<br /><br />Scott Evil: What? Are you feeding him? Why don't you just kill him?<br />Dr. Evil: I have an even better idea. I'm going to place him in an easily escapable situation involving an overly elaborate and exotic death.<br />Dr. Evil: All right guard, begin the unnecessarily slow-moving dipping mechanism.<br />[guard starts dipping mechanism:]<br />Dr. Evil: Close the tank!<br />Scott Evil: Wait, aren't you even going to watch them? They could get away!<br />Dr. Evil: No no no, I'm going to leave them alone and not actually witness them dying, I'm just gonna assume it all went to plan. What?<br />Scott Evil: I have a gun, in my room, you give me five seconds, I'll get it, I'll come back down here, BOOM, I'll blow their brains out!<br />Dr. Evil: Scott, you just don't get it, do ya? You don't. <br /><br />Now, I must sound very violent to some people. But seriously. This book has so many holes and plot lines that just don't make sense. It angers me.<br /><br />So, somebody take out the nasty violent children-attacking men. If I hear about one more electroshock, or welt on the head or split lip I'm going to call the publisher directly. PLEASE. Because I really have no more time for these shenanigans. <br /><br />(I apologize if you liked these books. I kept reading thinking they would get better. They never did. But maybe you will like them. The first part of the first book was the best. It was all downhill from there)</span>
  <a data-text-id="2168710708588650392" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

They become different in this book.<br/><br/>Sticky: Memorizes library catalogues.<br/>Reynie: Depelops sixth sense.<br/>Kate: Becomes The Flash.<br/>Constance: Becomes a mind reader. <br/><br/>Even though many unexplained mysteries unfold in this novel, the rest is pretty much boring.   <span id="freeText10110282764078115639" style="display:none">As much as I have enjoyed the first two novels in this series, I have felt exactly the opposite for this one. I simply can't recognize the characters I fell in love with. They become different in this book.<br /><br />Sticky: Memorizes library catalogues.<br />Reynie: Depelops sixth sense.<br />Kate: Becomes The Flash.<br />Constance: Becomes a mind reader. <br /><br />Even though many unexplained mysteries unfold in this novel, the rest is pretty much boring. The part till Constance's past being revealed was so dragged on that it took me a week to get through these pages. The children seemed to have lost their naturally magnificent ability and they act way beyond their characters. Even the adults were dully portrayed here.<br /><br />I became highly disapoined at the last instalment of my once favourite series. I wish the characters were a bit more lively here and the storyline a bit stronger.</span>

<div id="review_1881732100" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1881732100" />
    <a title="Jashan" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/59102077-jashan"><img alt="Jashan" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1546473140p2/59102077.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1881732100?book_show_action=true">Feb 18, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jashan" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jashan" href="/user/show/59102077-jashan">Jashan</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1881732100" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer348616200115077207">(Note: If you are planning to read this book and update on Goodreads, the updating format will be a bit strange. It will say that there are only nine pages in the book, meaning that you can only update one Goodreads page when you have really read about forty-three and a half pages in the actual book. This will make more sense once you read the book.) <br/><br/>Actual Review: I liked this book. I felt like the new plot was interesting, with the Stonetown blackout and all. But, I did have some problems, as </span>
  <span id="freeText348616200115077207" style="display:none">(Note: If you are planning to read this book and update on Goodreads, the updating format will be a bit strange. It will say that there are only nine pages in the book, meaning that you can only update one Goodreads page when you have really read about forty-three and a half pages in the actual book. This will make more sense once you read the book.) <br /><br />Actual Review: I liked this book. I felt like the new plot was interesting, with the Stonetown blackout and all. But, I did have some problems, as you can see in my deduction of two stars. My biggest one was the children themselves. That's right. Now, why would I have a grudge against the lovable Reynie, Kate, Sticky, and Constance? It's not because of their personalities, but because of their powers. I won't tell them - that would just ruin the fun. But, still, even though these powers show the aging of the Mysterious Benedict Society, the overall cleverness they possessed in the first and second books was almost diminished. Meaning, there aren't as many parts in the third book that would make you smile and feel guilty at the same time ("Wow, why couldn't I think of that?") as there were in the first and second books. <br />I was a bit disappointed with this book, as I expected a bit more from the ending of the series. Still, I would recommend this to anyone who enjoys kid-power books, not-too-violent reads, and, as a general rule, adventures in the contemporary world. <br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="348616200115077207" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_78005358" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/78005358" />
    <a title="Jelinas" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2297897-jelinas"><img alt="Jelinas" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1324389769p2/2297897.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/78005358?book_show_action=true">Nov 16, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jelinas" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jelinas" href="/user/show/2297897-jelinas">Jelinas</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer78005358" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8206929235368095203"><i>The Prisoner's Dilemma</i> is the third book in the <i>Mysterious Benedict Society</i> series. <br/><br/>For those not in the know, <i>The Mysterious Benedict Society</i> is a children's series by Trenton Lee Stewart. It follows the escapades of four specially gifted children as they work with their mentor, the wise and benevolent Nicholas Benedict, to thwart the plans of his evil twin brother, Ledroptha Curtain.<br/><br/>I think it’s easily the best new series to hit children’s lit since the Ramona books by Beverly Cleary (that’s r</span>
  <span id="freeText8206929235368095203" style="display:none"><i>The Prisoner's Dilemma</i> is the third book in the <i>Mysterious Benedict Society</i> series. <br /><br />For those not in the know, <i>The Mysterious Benedict Society</i> is a children's series by Trenton Lee Stewart. It follows the escapades of four specially gifted children as they work with their mentor, the wise and benevolent Nicholas Benedict, to thwart the plans of his evil twin brother, Ledroptha Curtain.<br /><br />I think it’s easily the best new series to hit children’s lit since the Ramona books by Beverly Cleary (that’s right, J.K. Rowling. I’m dismissing <i>Harry Potter</i> into the annals of crappy children’s lit – where it belongs) and the best mystery for kids since Ellen Raskin’s <i>The Westing Game</i>, which, in my mind, is the best children’s mystery novel of all time.<br /><br />The kids are usually somehow separated from all of their adult friends and must band together to figure out what Mr. Curtain is up to and stop it. Usually, the reader can play along by trying to decipher the clues that the <i>MBS</i> get.<br /><br />But my favorite thing about this series is not the mystery. No, that’s just the meat sauce covering up all the carrots and spinach that Mom snuck into the spaghetti. My favorite thing about Stewart’s series is that the kids are refreshingly <i>good</i>. <br /><br />I don’t know when it became okay and even respected for kids to sass their parents and treat one another like crap. Characters in books don’t <i>say</i> things anymore. They scream them. It’s like they’re constantly yelling at one another because of the terrible burden of whatever mission it is they’re trying to accomplish.<br /><br />But the kids in <i>MBS</i> only shout when they have to in order to be heard. They do get annoyed with each other, but they *gasp!* <i>do their best not to show their annoyance</i>. That’s, like… mature behavior! I hope to God that some of the celebutards out there will someday read these books and think to themselves, “Hmm, I should exercise some self-control every now and again.”<br /><br />And the kids don’t just refrain from treating one another badly. When one of them makes a mistake, instead of sniping at one another and pointing fingers, the others leap at the opportunity to encourage their teammate. Each of them has a different skill: Reynie is a critical thinker, Sticky has a photographic memory, Kate can climb anything and outrun most adults, and Constance has the gift of extraordinary stubbornness. Oh, and ESP.<br /><br />Each of them may have a special talent, but they all know that they need to work as a team in order to succeed. There’s no “lone wolf” mentality in these books. They encourage community and teamwork and friendship.<br /><br />In this specific installment of the series, the evil Mr. Curtain is after Constance for her ability to read and control minds. The plot involves a power outage, a showdown, and some fun clues to figure out (they’re doable if you’re well-versed in riddling). <br /><br />This installment was just okay, but the series as a whole still gets a solid rating from me.<br /><br />I’d highly recommend this series to anyone with kids ages nine or ten and up. Screw the wizards. I want to be a secret agent.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="8206929235368095203" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1699445511" />
    <a title="Star Shining Forever" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/17209879-star-shining-forever"><img alt="Star Shining Forever" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1366757251p2/17209879.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1699445511?book_show_action=true">Sep 24, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780316045506" href="/book/show/6973518-the-mysterious-benedict-society-and-the-prisoner-s-dilemma">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/17209879-star-shining-forever?shelf=modern-setting">modern-setting</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/17209879-star-shining-forever?shelf=cool-fiction">cool-fiction</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1699445511" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2494405979333359498">Now THIS is the Mysterious Benedict Society we know and love! No plodding travel, disobedient kids, and scarcity of riddles. Just our favorite characters saving the world the way they do best!<br/><br/>The opener is an enthralling real-life Prisoners Dilemma, with the Society locked in 2 attic rooms. Recapping and hashing through it brings to light that the children are all naturally loyal, possibly with the exception of the still cranky Constance, that Kate's physical prowess can still get them out of ju</span>
  <span id="freeText2494405979333359498" style="display:none">Now THIS is the Mysterious Benedict Society we know and love! No plodding travel, disobedient kids, and scarcity of riddles. Just our favorite characters saving the world the way they do best!<br /><br />The opener is an enthralling real-life Prisoners Dilemma, with the Society locked in 2 attic rooms. Recapping and hashing through it brings to light that the children are all naturally loyal, possibly with the exception of the still cranky Constance, that Kate's physical prowess can still get them out of just about any scrape, and that Reynie still excels at out-of-the-box problem solving.<br /><br />The Society, their parents, and Mr. Benedict's crew are essentially under house arrest in the Benedict manor as the government vigilantly watches over the Whisperer housed there while continuing in the fruitless search for Ledroptha Curtain. While chafing under the restrictions, the children welcome the opportunities to baffle and sneak past the guards, as well as spend this regular time with each other. Constance is brought to the forefront in an alarming way as, just as Mr. Benedict is about to adopt her, a stranger claims he is her father instead! This throws the household into a tizzy as measures are taken to refute this claim (also leading to the dubious finding that Constance previously survived by living in libraries), but unawares a dastardly plan of Mr. Curtain's is being put into action. <br /><br />Things soon kick into high gear. A blanket of darkness covers the city as all the electricity goes out! A wave of terror is unleashed as Curtain's Ten Men go out on the march in full force, seeking both the Whisperer and Constance for her mental powers. This time, the kids don't have to sneak off for the story to get anywhere, but there's a natural progression of story for the adults and kids to get separated and each shine in their own talents and abilities. In search of Constance, escaping from the Ten Men, and traveling the darkened streets: the Society does it all together. <br /><br />The stakes are heightened and the ante is upped with the extra sneakiness of Mr. Curtain and the Ten Men. By now, they know the Society and the kids they're up against. Reynie utilizes his cleverness, Kate's agility, and Sticky's knowledge in deciphering secret messages, brainstorming solutions, and executing retaliations. But the bad guys have a few tricks up their sleeves, making everything much more scary and exciting!<br /><br />A standoff against the Ten Men does not end well this time. The kids' out-of-the-box solution to the Prisoners Dilemma comes in handy against the cruel fiends, and they'll need all their quick thinking and swift action to help themselves and Milligan (laughably underequipped as always) out of the stickiest situations yet.</span>
  <a data-text-id="2494405979333359498" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_332722814" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/332722814" />
    <a title="Cindy" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2058617-cindy"><img alt="Cindy" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1576473595p2/2058617.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/332722814?book_show_action=true">May 19, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Cindy" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Cindy" href="/user/show/2058617-cindy">Cindy</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer332722814" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12786396363975658276">In this supposedly last book of the MBS series, I thought it was very clever how the title was incorporated into the story. Mr. Benedict continues to try and stimulate the superior intellects of his young charges, and is always giving them clever mind games and puzzles to solve. In the opening pages, the four kids are divided into two teams and presented with a "Prisoner's Dilemma"--they are given 3 scenarios with different consequences, and each team must decide not only which scenario they wou</span>
  <span id="freeText12786396363975658276" style="display:none">In this supposedly last book of the MBS series, I thought it was very clever how the title was incorporated into the story. Mr. Benedict continues to try and stimulate the superior intellects of his young charges, and is always giving them clever mind games and puzzles to solve. In the opening pages, the four kids are divided into two teams and presented with a "Prisoner's Dilemma"--they are given 3 scenarios with different consequences, and each team must decide not only which scenario they would prefer, but try to figure out what the other team would decide, because the fate of each determines the fate of all! It reminded me of scenes from a cop show, where two suspects are places in different interrogation rooms in the hopes that one will 'rat out' the other, and the truth will be obtained! Now, granted, the children's consequence was related to after-dinner chores, but the concept was a thought-provoking exercise, and it served them well once their next challenge appeared! Mr. Benedict has been working intensely to try and modify the dreaded "Chair" so that its mind-reading and mind-altering properties can be changed. But then the chair is stolen, and the Mysterious Benedict Society decides to set out on their own to recover it! Once again, they go up against the dreaded "Ten Men" in an attempt to outsmart them and recover the chair before Mr. Curtain can use it to bend the minds of the world to his will! "What are we gonna do tonight, Brain?" "The same thing we do every night, Pinky....try to take over the world!" (Thanks, Animaniacs!) All of these books are fun because the reader is expected to try and puzzle out the clues and problems that the characters face. My brain was tested on logic puzzles, secret codes and trying to remember hints that were given to figure out the next steps! I highly recommend these books for mature 4th/5th grade readers and middle schoolers, especially those with analytic/logical minds! </span>
  <a data-text-id="12786396363975658276" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer14018464099217409268">I enjoyed this one so much, as always. Such an amazing book and series! This book has been the perfect ending to the Mysterious Benedict Society trilogy and series for so long, and I love it. It's strange but awesome to know that later this month, it will no longer be the last one.<br/><br/>One of my favorite aspects of the series is seeing the children and their families work as an inseparable team, relying on each other and working together. I love how they choose each other as best friends and surrogat</span>
  <span id="freeText14018464099217409268" style="display:none">I enjoyed this one so much, as always. Such an amazing book and series! This book has been the perfect ending to the Mysterious Benedict Society trilogy and series for so long, and I love it. It's strange but awesome to know that later this month, it will no longer be the last one.<br /><br />One of my favorite aspects of the series is seeing the children and their families work as an inseparable team, relying on each other and working together. I love how they choose each other as best friends and surrogate family members, and how the four children work so well together. And I love how they're unofficially adopted into Mr. Benedict's family--along with their parents! It's so heartwarming and wonderful to watch them live as one large, loving family. Chosen surrogate families in books are one of my favorite things. And Mysterious Benedict Society also has a theme of actual adoption in a legal sense, and every other sense--something I'm passionate about, so I love seeing it celebrated in this way.<br /><br />Of course, I've continued to enjoy the individual children and their individual relationships, as well as their united dynamic. And I love that we get to see more of Constance in this third book--finding out more about her, her past, and her abilities. And the children's character arcs are always awesome, especially Reynie's.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="14018464099217409268" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <a title="Ensiform" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3843117-ensiform"><img alt="Ensiform" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1275973241p2/3843117.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/128578277?book_show_action=true">Oct 30, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Ensiform" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Ensiform" href="/user/show/3843117-ensiform">Ensiform</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3843117-ensiform?shelf=fiction">fiction</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer128578277" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13717039506988053317">In their third adventure, the Society (and powerful machine known as the Whisperer) are under heavy guard at Mr. Benedict's house. The government wants the machine, as does the nasty Mr. Curtain, who is not above kidnapping the children to get it. Fearing the worst and frightened by her new mental powers, Constance runs away; it is then that Curtain’s Ten Men strike, and the children are on their own, hoping to save the day. <br/><br/>As with the previous entries in this series, I enjoyed immensely the mi</span>
  <span id="freeText13717039506988053317" style="display:none">In their third adventure, the Society (and powerful machine known as the Whisperer) are under heavy guard at Mr. Benedict's house. The government wants the machine, as does the nasty Mr. Curtain, who is not above kidnapping the children to get it. Fearing the worst and frightened by her new mental powers, Constance runs away; it is then that Curtain’s Ten Men strike, and the children are on their own, hoping to save the day. <br /><br />As with the previous entries in this series, I enjoyed immensely the mind puzzles, the codes, the scenes of peril and adventure. There's truly something for every youthful reader to admire here: those who yearn for stories of athleticism and bravery and those who like more cerebral heroes. With the mental faculties Constance develops in this book, there’s now a supernatural element as well. And as before, Steward fully realizes every character, giving Curtain and his bungling assistant S.Q. motive and method. They don’t think of themselves as "bad guys," as S.Q. explains. They’re trying to do what they think is best, even if Curtain thinks certain ends justify rather costly means. The sheer novelty has worn off, but this is another well-written, thoughtful, amusing adventure.</span>
  <a data-text-id="13717039506988053317" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer4369470896276258410">Four and a half stars, actually.<br/> The wit so prevalent in the first book has diminished and is almost non-existent.<br/> The plot significantly improved from book 2. Even though I never quite figured out what exactly Mr. Curtain was planning (maybe I was just reading too fast for my brain to register the necessary details), it still was good. *spoiler/* I did NOT see the trap baited with clues coming! */spoiler*<br/> Constance is back to her normal self, as is Reynie.<br/> I mentioned that Milligan is amazing. </span>
  <span id="freeText4369470896276258410" style="display:none">Four and a half stars, actually.<br /> The wit so prevalent in the first book has diminished and is almost non-existent.<br /> The plot significantly improved from book 2. Even though I never quite figured out what exactly Mr. Curtain was planning (maybe I was just reading too fast for my brain to register the necessary details), it still was good. *spoiler/* I did NOT see the trap baited with clues coming! */spoiler*<br /> Constance is back to her normal self, as is Reynie.<br /> I mentioned that Milligan is amazing. Well, so is McCracken. Please don't scream in rage and horror. I will explain. They are both similar; calm in the middle of a pencil-throwing contest, and even making jokes. It's a bit (understatement) unnerving. What makes them so shockingly different is their drive: Milligan goes for justice while McCracken goes for money. That's what makes one totally honorable and the other absolutely ignoble.<br /> I really like Mr. Curtain and S. Q.'s relationship, and the way it was resolved. Though it is rather strange.<br /> By the way, I wasn't quite as annoyed when Connie developed telepathy as I was when she got the ultra-sensitive stuff in book 2. I love her poem about green plaid. I didn't laughed as much as Mr. Benedict, but then again, nobody can (now that the nasty narcolepsy is gone).<br /> *spoiler/* Pencilla. Ha, ha. Love it. */spoiler*<br /> And I love the ending.</span>

    <a title="Megan Miller" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/36209961-megan-miller"><img alt="Megan Miller" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1603830205p2/36209961.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3538083798?book_show_action=true">Sep 17, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Megan Miller" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Megan Miller" href="/user/show/36209961-megan-miller">Megan Miller</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback " href="/book/show/25134664-the-mysterious-benedict-society-and-the-prisoner-s-dilemma">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3538083798" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer772974827500434262">I perhaps spent a good bit more time reading this today than I ought to have. There are dishes to be washed and meals to be cooked, after all!<br/><br/>But alas, remembering grown-up things while reading Mysterious Benedict Society is harder than it seems.<br/><br/>These are good adventures. I will read them to my children someday and we will talk of the mishaps and mayhem. We will make friends anew with the golden characters and learn the bittersweet feeling of happy endings and moving on.</span>

          </span>
        </div>


      <div class="reviewFooter uitext buttons">

<div id="review_375353361" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/375353361" />
    <a title="Hannah" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/6334281-hannah"><img alt="Hannah" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1597962197p2/6334281.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/375353361?book_show_action=true">Jul 23, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Hannah" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Hannah" href="/user/show/6334281-hannah">Hannah</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer375353361" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16935334428369225797">I was sadly disappointed by this book. In book one and two all of the characters grow and mature in someway or another. However, in this final installment I felt that there was very little maturing at all. I loved Constance in the other books, her actions seemed appropriate for her age and she even grew up quite a bit. However, in this final book she's four years old and she acts like she is once again a two year old. It would have been fine if he had left her age at three-I can fathom a three y</span>
  <span id="freeText16935334428369225797" style="display:none">I was sadly disappointed by this book. In book one and two all of the characters grow and mature in someway or another. However, in this final installment I felt that there was very little maturing at all. I loved Constance in the other books, her actions seemed appropriate for her age and she even grew up quite a bit. However, in this final book she's four years old and she acts like she is once again a two year old. It would have been fine if he had left her age at three-I can fathom a three year old occasionally acting like a two year old or a four year old acting like a three year old-but when a child is young like that- two years at that age is a HUGE difference! <br /><br />I felt that this book also focused too much on just Constance. The other characters seemed just thrown in there- an afterthought. The balance between the four of them is what attracted me to the books in the first place. I do not feel that this book should not have been titled the Mysterious Benedict Society- it should have been titled "Constance Contraire- and the people at her beck and call." I did NOT like the new Constance! Giving her Mind Control seemed a like a terrible way to handle things. I liked the fact that she could figure out patterns of what was going to happen next in book two- it seemed like a feasible, realistic, and intelligent decision. I felt that giving a child like her mind control was a foolish idea- she already has enough demons to deal with (ie her temper, laziness and impatience) with out adding that on top of it. Giving her mind control villianized her, in more ways than one, first- Mr. Stewart undermined one of the very important principles that was so highly elaborated upon in book one and two- freedom of thought and freedom from being controlled. So it was ok, for a willful four year old to use it to her advantage, but not Mr. Curtain, our main villain? I'm not just talking about the Ice Cream incident- I'm referring to using it against her enemies as well. It defeated the whole mission of the Benedict Society. <br /><br />Another element that suffered, due to the lack of foresight on the part of the author, was the plot. Because Constance was given mind control it made their escapes a lot less ingenious and harrowing. It was lazy and this book was rushed. Don't get me wrong- I loved the first two books. However, in my opinion the reader would be better off just reading the first two and imagining that our characters lived happily ever after, rather than read this sad excuse for a conclusion. I will probably read the prequel though, given the enormous amount of talent that was obvious in the first two books. </span>
  <a data-text-id="16935334428369225797" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

                    This review has been hidden because it contains spoilers. To view it,

              <span id="reviewTextContainer150832950" class="readable"
                    style="display:none"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6879076144702499125">The Mysterious Benedict Society is a society that consists of the smartest children: Reynie, Stickie, Constance and Kate. They are part of Mr. Benedict's secret society that stops his twin brother from creating trouble in the world. In previous books, Mr. Benedict's brother, Mr. Leodroptha Curtain, created a horrible machine called, "The Whisperer." It brainwashes you and makes you forget your memories. When you forget those memories, Mr. Curtain takes advantage of you and turns you bad. The poi</span>
  <span id="freeText6879076144702499125" style="display:none">The Mysterious Benedict Society is a society that consists of the smartest children: Reynie, Stickie, Constance and Kate. They are part of Mr. Benedict's secret society that stops his twin brother from creating trouble in the world. In previous books, Mr. Benedict's brother, Mr. Leodroptha Curtain, created a horrible machine called, "The Whisperer." It brainwashes you and makes you forget your memories. When you forget those memories, Mr. Curtain takes advantage of you and turns you bad. The point of this society is so that they can stop Mr. Curtain from using it. Fortunately this machine is under Mr. Benedict's hand. Unfortunately, his brother and his men, The Executives, are trying to take it away from horrible uses.<br />In this book, the adventure begins when Constance runs away from home. At that same time, there's a horrible blackout in the whole city. The children are left at home when the adults go look for Constance. The Executives go to the house and take The Whisperer. The men leave a clue behind accidentally, causing them to go find and stop the evil men. <br />In the end, the kids find Constance, but they get caught by The Executives. Constance realizes that she can see and send visions to/from people. She sends a vision to Mr. Benedict telling him where they are and he sends one back saying help is on the way. At the end, the children are saved and The Whisperer is back in Mr. Benedict's hands.<br />I LOVE this series. There are so many riddles in this book that will get you thinking. I haven't solved any of them on my own without looking forward. These books are more of books for the teenage age. Younger kids probably won't get it. If you are younger than me and you get it, I applaud you. I love Milligan. He always seems like he can win a fight without using much violence. He is definitely smart and very very strategic. He risked his life for his kid. He is a father that I would totally want in my life. (JK, I love you dad!)</span>

    <a title="Spencer Brokaw" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5692113-spencer-brokaw"><img alt="Spencer Brokaw" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/m_50x66-82093808bca726cb3249a493fbd3bd0f.png" /></a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Spencer Brokaw" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Spencer Brokaw" href="/user/show/5692113-spencer-brokaw">Spencer Brokaw</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer320141915" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15898481161836353259"> I recently read The Mysterious Benedict Society and the Prisoner's Dilemma, the third and final book in the trilogy. The story focuses on extraordinarily smart kids Reynie, Sticky, Constance, and Kate. When the power goes off in the city of Stonetown, the children investigate and problems begin to arise. Out of the books, I'd say this is my second favorite, the first being my least. The books gradually got better, although the plot isn't as strong as the second book, which remains my all-time f</span>
  <span id="freeText15898481161836353259" style="display:none"> I recently read The Mysterious Benedict Society and the Prisoner's Dilemma, the third and final book in the trilogy. The story focuses on extraordinarily smart kids Reynie, Sticky, Constance, and Kate. When the power goes off in the city of Stonetown, the children investigate and problems begin to arise. Out of the books, I'd say this is my second favorite, the first being my least. The books gradually got better, although the plot isn't as strong as the second book, which remains my all-time favorite of the series. This book is filled with action, and closes the series nicely. The book reeled me in within the first chapter, and I was hooked until the end. I liked the description in the book, and thought it did a nice job describing everything. There wasn't much character development in this book, but a few things are revealed at the end. <br /><br />Sometimes the book got a little dull, but the book picked up pace and the story gradually got more exciting. I am pleased with the series, and glad that I read it. I'm looking forward to the prequel series, with hope that it will answer a few more questions. I give this book a 4/5.</span>
  <a data-text-id="15898481161836353259" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <a title="Lsk" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3931689-lsk"><img alt="Lsk" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/u_50x66-632230dc9882b4352d753eedf9396530.png" /></a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Lsk" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Lsk" href="/user/show/3931689-lsk">Lsk</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer108967659" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9548641071633161739"><br/><br/>I was just reading a negative review of The Mysterious Benedict Society and felt a wave of consensus rushing over me. I have a 9-year old daughter who keeps falling asleep when I read her this book. While she was away for the weekend, I finished it and thought I understood the problem: it's written for the parents not the kids, at least the parents who want to feel clever for grasping a plot about 'grown-up' problems like bureaucracy, mind-control, and subliminal messages. Far superior to this s</span>
  <span id="freeText9548641071633161739" style="display:none"><br /><br />I was just reading a negative review of The Mysterious Benedict Society and felt a wave of consensus rushing over me. I have a 9-year old daughter who keeps falling asleep when I read her this book. While she was away for the weekend, I finished it and thought I understood the problem: it's written for the parents not the kids, at least the parents who want to feel clever for grasping a plot about 'grown-up' problems like bureaucracy, mind-control, and subliminal messages. Far superior to this series, in my opinion, is Ellen Potter's Olivia Kidney, which is genuinely brilliant storytelling, with eccentric characters and imaginative set-pieces, as much allusion as an adult could want to mythology and literary tradition, at the same time it leaves indelible traces for a child's imagination to safekeep. I wish the movie industry would pick *this* book up, as it's a wonderful detour from the Harry Potter/Unfortunate Events formulae, which the Benedict Society merely repeats in a more adult-friendly form.<br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="9548641071633161739" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('5mcXRyN145tfm6HU4NKT28ePYfQKacFJiWrYrZB3BDYTJtWjvgtcPOoYZQf1CyV6rMbYvvFE63u0+ITIyro8YA==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }
